[14:30:01.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:30:02.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:31:00.0000] <Hixie>

[14:31:03.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:32:00.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:32:01.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:32:02.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:33:02.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:34:01.0000] <Hixie>

[14:34:02.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:35:00.0000] <Hixie>
well it's kind of networking -- LOADING means you haven't received enough data yet to know if you'll go to ERROR or not

[14:35:01.0000] <Hixie>
BUFFERING means you've received enough data to know you're happy and to have initialised the rest of the object

[14:37:00.0000] <Hixie>

[14:37:01.0000] <Hixie>
where EMPTY becomes effectively useless

[14:37:02.0000] <othermaciej>
EMPTY means you can't do anything

[14:37:03.0000] <Hixie>

[14:38:00.0000] <othermaciej>

[14:38:01.0000] <othermaciej>
much like the network-related EMPTY state

[14:38:02.0000] <Hixie>

[14:38:03.0000] <othermaciej>
you can switch back to EMPTY?

[14:38:04.0000] <Hixie>
i don't really like making the second one parially random-access but partially ordered

[14:39:00.0000] <Hixie>
sure, EMPTY is just "i don't have a frame or anything for this playback position"

[14:39:01.0000] <othermaciej>
I think it is overly simplistic to say state machines must either be linear or always allow transition to all states

[14:39:02.0000] <othermaciej>
I mean, you couldn't build a coke machine with those constraints

[14:39:03.0000] <Hixie>
they don't have to

[14:39:04.0000] <Hixie>
but it makes it way simpler if they do :-)

[14:39:05.0000] <othermaciej>
and that's the canonical example of a simple state machine

[14:39:06.0000] <othermaciej>
simpler for who?

[14:39:07.0000] <othermaciej>
the spec author, who can get out of drawing a state transition diagram?

[14:40:00.0000] <Hixie>
authors to understand, me to spec, implementors to follow...

[14:40:01.0000] <gsnedders>
it's easier to understand when implementing

[14:40:02.0000] <othermaciej>
when implementing, you have to understand every single transition arc

[14:40:03.0000] <Hixie>
right, so it's simpler if those are easyto enumerate

[14:41:00.0000] <othermaciej>
if you can go from any state to any other, that's n^2-n transition arcs

[14:41:01.0000] <Hixie>
there are no more transitions in your proposal (METADATA in readyState) than mine (METADATA in networkState)

[14:41:02.0000] <othermaciej>
that is in fact maximal complexity for an n-state machine, not minimal

[14:42:00.0000] <Hixie>
our proposals have the same number of transitions

[14:42:01.0000] <othermaciej>
sure, I'm just debating the premise that a "random access" state machine is somehow good for implementors

[14:42:02.0000] <Hixie>
i'm not saying that

[14:43:00.0000] <Hixie>
i'm saying that two state machines one of which is purely linear and the other of which is purely random-access is better than two state machines where one is linear and the other is bigger than the random access one, adding one extra arc that isn't random access

[14:44:00.0000] <othermaciej>
and I think if you want to partition state, you should do it by how the state will be used and what it represents, not by what the state transitions look like

[14:45:00.0000] <Hixie>
that's actually what i said originally when you originally suggested that

[14:45:01.0000] <Hixie>
i think having METADATA in the network state is more useful

[14:45:02.0000] <othermaciej>
[ EMPTY --> LOADING --> METADATA --> LOADED ] doesn't make logical sense

[14:46:00.0000] <Hixie>
[ EMPTY -> opening connection -> received metadata -> receiving data -> received all ] makes logical sense

[14:46:01.0000] <Hixie>
however, one argument against this is you'd never stay in the metadata state

[14:46:02.0000] <othermaciej>
it would if "receiving metadata" was actually a separate step

[14:47:00.0000] <othermaciej>
but having the metadata is a side effect of being in the "I'm transferring bytes now" step, not a separate operation

[14:47:01.0000] <Dashiva>
But the "all metadata available" event would be useful, so it has to get into there somehow

[14:48:00.0000] <Hixie>
that's a point

[14:48:01.0000] <Hixie>
having it in the readyState means you'll get that message more often

[14:48:02.0000] <Hixie>
though

[14:48:03.0000] <Hixie>
no

[14:48:04.0000] <othermaciej>
you'll get it any time you seek to a place where you don't have a frame ready immediately

[14:48:05.0000] <Hixie>
we could just say that when you don't get the BUFFERING state until you have the metadata

[14:48:06.0000] <Hixie>
s/when//

[14:48:07.0000] <othermaciej>
but otherwise you would have gotten the readyState EMPTY state then

[14:49:00.0000] <Dashiva>
Or make metadataLoaded a separate boolean with associated event... mhrr

[14:49:01.0000] <Hixie>
actually we can get rid of this step altogether if we have the states split....

[14:50:00.0000] <Hixie>
you just define BUFFERING to happen only after you have metadata

[14:50:01.0000] <Hixie>
then you're set

[14:50:02.0000] <othermaciej>
I'm not sure what that means or how it is different than what the doc says now

[14:51:00.0000] <Hixie>
/me gets himself really confused

[14:51:01.0000] <Hixie>
i just went through three arguments in a row that put me straight back to where i was initially

[14:51:02.0000] <Hixie>
i am not dizzy

[14:51:03.0000] <Hixie>
now

[14:51:04.0000] <othermaciej>
you have [ EMPTY -> LOADING -> BUFFERING -> LOADED ] right now

[14:52:00.0000] <Hixie>
right. that's what i think we want. EMPTY = nothing done. LOADING = sent request. BUFFERING = got back metadata, other fields now are initialised. LOADED = all data now downloaded, you can go offline safely.

[14:52:01.0000] <othermaciej>
I think LOADING vs. BUFFERING is descriptively poor as a way to say whether you have the metadata, and I think having the metadata belongs logically with presentability state, not networking state

[14:52:02.0000] <Hixie>
LOADING doesn't mean you have the metadata

[14:52:03.0000] <Hixie>
LOADING means you don't have anything, but you've requested it

[14:52:04.0000] <othermaciej>
LOADING means you don't have the metadata

[14:52:05.0000] <Hixie>
SENT maybe would be better

[14:52:06.0000] <othermaciej>
BUFFERING means you do

[14:53:00.0000] <othermaciej>
that is the only difference

[14:53:01.0000] <othermaciej>
otherwise they both mean you are receiving some octets over the network

[14:53:02.0000] <Hixie>
right.

[14:53:03.0000] <Hixie>
so what's wrong with that?

[14:54:00.0000] <othermaciej>
the names of the states have no relation to this distinction

[14:54:01.0000] <othermaciej>
and in fact sound like synonyms

[14:54:02.0000] <Hixie>
i'm open to new names

[14:54:03.0000] <othermaciej>
(because from a purely networking POV, they are)

[14:55:00.0000] <Dashiva>
So you will be in BUFFERING state even if you're playing back with fast enough download to never enter buffering mode before end?

[14:55:01.0000] <Hixie>
i thought we weren't discussing names yet :-)

[14:55:02.0000] <othermaciej>
I think the problem with the names is because they are trying to draw a distinction that, from the point of view of networking, does not exist

[14:55:03.0000] <Hixie>
/me changes the names to EMPTY SENT LOADING LOADED

[14:55:04.0000] <Dashiva>
FINISHED :)

[14:56:00.0000] <Hixie>
finished, like language, initialised, and various other words, are bad in APIs because people mistype them too much

[14:56:01.0000] <othermaciej>
SENT vs. LOADING is misleading, since you might take it to mean that in SENT state you have not received any bytes yet

[14:56:02.0000] <othermaciej>
which is not the distinction it is trying to draw

[14:57:00.0000] <othermaciej>
seriously, having the metadata or not is a presnetability issue not a networking issue

[14:57:01.0000] <othermaciej>
putting it into the readyState immediately makes it super clear, for this reason

[14:57:02.0000] <Hixie>
UNSENT, SENT, RECEIVING, DONE? that's what XHR uses.

[14:57:03.0000] <othermaciej>
it's true that you can't go back to not having metadata

[14:57:04.0000] <Hixie>
it totally is a network issue

[14:58:00.0000] <Hixie>
until you have this part of the data, nothing else makes any sense

[14:58:01.0000] <othermaciej>
it is no more a network issue than having the first frame is a network issue

[14:58:02.0000] <Hixie>
except that you can go and lose the first frame

[14:58:03.0000] <Dashiva>
/me wonders about mistyping finished

[14:58:04.0000] <Hixie>
but you can never lose the metadata

[14:59:00.0000] <othermaciej>
whether you can lose that level of presentability is not in any way due to networking

[14:59:01.0000] <othermaciej>
it's because having a frame is dependent on where you are on the timeline

[15:00:00.0000] <Hixie>
granted, but i don't see why that matters. how is having it in the attribute that tells you the state of frame playbackability useful?

[15:01:00.0000] <Hixie>
it seems to me that having the metadata is closer to the network state (it's a milestone along the download) than it is to the seeking and decoding state

[15:01:01.0000] <othermaciej>
that's the state you normally need to track to know what state to put the controls in

[15:02:00.0000] <Hixie>
controls don't disable themselves just because you're not able to play the current frame in current UIs

[15:03:00.0000] <Hixie>
they enable themselves once, when you have enough data to know wtf you're looking at

[15:03:01.0000] <othermaciej>
it's really only the first transition to having a frame that significantly matters, really

[15:04:00.0000] <othermaciej>
since most things only show placeholder UI before you have the first frame, when you seek they usually stick on the last frame seen

[15:04:01.0000] <Hixie>
agreed

[15:05:00.0000] <Hixie>
/me ponders on this

[15:08:00.0000] <Hixie>
(on names, HAVE_FRAME doesn't really work for audio)

[15:08:01.0000] <othermaciej>
that state isn't really relevant to pure audio

[15:09:00.0000] <othermaciej>
since audio is more purely time-based, there's no such thing as presenting a static view of the current time

[15:10:00.0000] <Hixie>
there could be (e.g. embedded static images, captions, visualisation)

[15:12:00.0000] <othermaciej>
a static image along the lines of cover art would be considered metadata, not a playable track

[15:12:01.0000] <othermaciej>
if there is a text track displayed as captions, it's probably reasonable to consider each piece of text a "frame"

[15:13:00.0000] <othermaciej>
probably better than calling the state CAN_SHOW_STATIC_VIEW_OF_CURRENT_TIME

[23:17:00.0000] <Hixie>
introducing a new status to mean "not completely loaded but partialy loaded and we're not going to bother getting more" seems like more work than it's worth

[23:17:01.0000] <Hixie>
(for implementors and authors)

[23:17:02.0000] <Hixie>

[23:17:03.0000] <Hixie>
which seems poor

[23:23:00.0000] <Hixie>
this sucks

[23:23:01.0000] <Hixie>
having a network problem or user cancelation nearly arbitrarily result in a LOADED or an ERROR is stupid

[23:24:00.0000] <Hixie>
in the former case there's no way to catch the error if joining late, e.g.

[23:24:01.0000] <Hixie>
but we can't use the same code as otherwise you can't tell if the other attributes are safe

[23:24:02.0000] <Hixie>
maybe we should just have a lastError attribute

[23:24:03.0000] <Hixie>
which is reset when you get a successful transition

[23:24:04.0000] <Hixie>
or rather, is reset by load()

[23:25:00.0000] <Hixie>
or maybe when we have an error or abort we should leave the state in its last state and set an error flag

[23:25:01.0000] <othermaciej>
I'm not sure you should go to LOADED on a user cancel or late error - probably better to stay in current state with alternate way to get the error (like lastError)

[23:25:02.0000] <Hixie>
that way you can see where the error occured

[23:26:00.0000] <othermaciej>
that might obviate the need for an ERROR state I guess

what besides entering non-playable state or reaching the end?

[23:57:00.0000] <Hixie>
currently: seeking (UNAVAILABLE and paused=false and seeking=true), buffering (UNAVAILABLE or CAN_SHOW_CURRENT_FRAME and paused=false and seeking=false, playback position isn't in the buffered range), ended is true, and a fatal error occured, either network error or during decoding.

[23:58:00.0000] <Hixie>
currently the first two will fire a 'waiting' event when they occur, the latter two won't.

[23:58:01.0000] <othermaciej>
fatal error partway should arguably count as truncating the duration

[23:59:00.0000] <KevinMarks>

[23:59:01.0000] <Hixie>

[23:59:02.0000] <Hixie>
not sure we care about that though

[15:44:04.0000] <Hixie>
23:17 <         Hixie>|when someone changes the <video src=""> and invokes .load() again, what should happen?

[15:44:05.0000] <Hixie>
23:17 <         Hixie>|should everything reset to initial values?

[15:44:06.0000] <Hixie>
23:17 <         Hixie>|should events be fired for each attribute that's reset?

[15:46:00.0000] <Hixie>
in particular, right load you invoke a load() method to restart the video element with a new source

[15:46:01.0000] <Hixie>
but that needs to fire a whole sequence of events: abort on the previous thing, emptied because we're going back to zero, paused if it was previously playing, unavailable if we had a frame before, begin to indicate we've started a new download

[15:47:00.0000] <Hixie>
and i'm not really sure what order those events should fire in, and whether they should fire before or after load() returns

[15:48:00.0000] <Hixie>
it feels like 'abort' should fire after it returns, but it also feels like the attributes should be reset before it returns, and it feels like they should be reset after abort is fired

[15:48:01.0000] <Hixie>
which is an overconstrained situation

[15:48:02.0000] <Hixie>
we could just say that you can't re-use a <video> but that seems dumb

[15:48:03.0000] <Hixie>
i think i'm going to think on this while cycling to work. feel free to describe your thoughts here and i'll read them when i get in.

[17:11:00.0000] <Hixie>
ok we're gonna synchronously fire an 'abort' event while load() is running, followed by an 'emptied' event.

[17:11:01.0000] <Hixie>
the next questios whether to fire the 'begin' event before or after the method returns

[17:11:02.0000] <Hixie>
and whether to set the state to LOADING before or after the method returns

[17:11:03.0000] <Hixie>

[17:12:00.0000] <Hixie>

[17:12:01.0000] <Hixie>

[17:59:02.0000] <Philip`>
I think this works around that html5lib problem:

[17:59:03.0000] <Philip`>
    import xml.dom.minidom

[17:59:04.0000] <Philip`>
    import html5lib

[17:59:05.0000] <Philip`>
    parser = html5lib.html5parser.HTMLParser(tree=html5lib.treebuilders.dom.TreeBuilder)

[17:59:06.0000] <Philip`>
    doc = parser.parse(open('current-work'), encoding='utf-8')

[17:59:07.0000] <Philip`>
    doc.removeChild(doc.firstChild) # remove the doctype, else html5lib's doc.cloneNode dies

[17:59:08.0000] <Philip`>
    head = doc.documentElement.getElementsByTagName('head')[0]

[17:59:09.0000] <Philip`>
    head.insertBefore(doc.createElement('meta'), head.firstChild).setAttribute('charset', 'UTF-8')

[17:59:10.0000] <Philip`>
...as a replacement for the top of the file

[17:59:11.0000] <Philip`>

[17:56:00.0000] <Philip`>
deltab: It parses it into a DOM, then extracts the common header/etc bits, then it keeps moving bits from the original single page into the new output page, and it starts a new output page when it reaches certain points (mostly <h2>/<h3>), and when it's finished it goes through every page and finds every ID, then it goes through every page and updates the links, and then it serialises everything out to HTML, and that's about

[17:56:01.0000] <Philip`>
... it.

[17:58:00.0000] <deltab>
ah, DOM + 1.5 MB source

[17:59:00.0000] <Philip`>
+ Python :-)

[17:59:01.0000] <Hixie>
my update script now calls a web service on w3.org to create the big index page, then calls a web service on a server i have access to in the UK to split the spec up, and that web service calls a web service on whatwg.org to fetch the resulting tarball and unzip it, and then the original script goes ahead and does a svn diff.

[06:59:00.0000] <Lachy>
I think the logic is this:...

[07:00:00.0000] <Lachy>
1. <!DOCTYPE html PUBLIC "html5"> triggers HTML5 mode, which will eventually become a frozen bug state

[07:00:01.0000] <Lachy>
2. After it becomes a frozen bug state, IE introduces another form of explicit opt-in. e.g. <html ie-version="9">

[07:01:00.0000] <Lachy>
3. IE continues updating the bug mode switch with each new release for several years, each time improving their compliance

[07:02:00.0000] <Lachy>
4. HTML6 is released a while after that with a new DOCTYPE. <!DOCTYPE html PUBLIC "html6">

[07:02:01.0000] <Lachy>
5. That provides a brand new opt-in, and by that time IE will be compliant enough to not need a specific bug mode opt-in

[07:07:00.0000] <Philip`>

[07:17:00.0000] <Philip`>
Lachy: Python 2.5 adds the keyword "with", but it's disabled by default (since it would break compatibility with existing code that uses variables/etc named "with")

[07:17:01.0000] <Philip`>
In Python 2.6, it will be enabled by default, so those programs have to be fixed before then

[07:17:02.0000] <Philip`>
In the meantime, Python 2.5 programs can write "from __future__ import with" to get the 2.6-like behaviour

[12:17:00.0000] <jdandrea>
Reality check Q (read: "I could be reading this incorrectly.") In section 3.2.3.6, is the "(e.g. no space characters)" at odds with major steps 4 and 6?

[12:18:00.0000] <jdandrea>
Put another way, is "1, 2, 3, 4" a valid list of integers or must it be "1,2,3,4"?

[12:19:00.0000] <Philip`>
As I read it, that's the difference between author conformance and UA conformance

[12:20:00.0000] <Philip`>
Authors must write that list as "1,2,3,4", but UAs must parse the invalid string "1, 2, 3, 4" in the same way

[12:21:00.0000] <jdandrea>
Ahh, I see - author it the former way, but forgive the spaces (or a leading comma) when parsing.

[12:25:00.0000] <Philip`>
Excepting any mistakes I've made, ",,,01,2.5--,3 , 4!" would be parsed the same way too

[13:56:00.0000] <Philip`>
C99 says "Physical source file multibyte characters are mapped, in an implementation-defined manner, to the source character set (introducing new-line characters for end-of-line indicators) if necessary."

[13:56:01.0000] <Philip`>
so that's not undefined behaviour

[13:57:00.0000] <zcorpan>
just implementation-defined?

[13:58:00.0000] <othermaciej>
implementation-defined behavior is undefined, if you assume it is being done in some specific way

[13:58:01.0000] <othermaciej>
for instance, assuming your physical source is UTF-16 and is translated to a source character set of UTF-8 would be wrong

[13:58:02.0000] <Philip`>
The source character set is letters, digits, and 29 graphic characters, and some whitespace

[13:58:03.0000] <Philip`>
"If any other characters are encountered in a source file (except in an identifier, a character constant, a string literal, a header name, a comment, or a preprocessing token that is never converted to a token), the behavior is undefined."

[13:59:00.0000] <zcorpan>

[08:22:00.0000] <zcorpan_>
ddfreyne: i think there are several reasons for using elements rather than attributes for article &c

[08:23:00.0000] <zcorpan_>
ddfreyne: (1) it's easier to author and maintain markup with element names instead of lots of divs

[08:24:00.0000] <zcorpan_>
ddfreyne: (2) if we continue reusing div for anything new this way we would end up with DivML 1.0 or something after a while

[08:25:00.0000] <zcorpan_>
ddfreyne: (3) it prevents the case where an element is both an article and nav at the same time, or where the attribute is placed on bogus places

[08:25:01.0000] <ddfreyne>
zcorpan_: (1) You could keep on adding new elements for anything that is used a lot

[08:26:00.0000] <ddfreyne>
zcorpan_: (2) using new elements breaks in some browsers, while role=... or class=... does not

[08:26:01.0000] <ddfreyne>
and I have no 3 yet

[08:26:02.0000] <zcorpan_>
ddfreyne: (4) it's more performant to process elements than attributes in the general case (look at the headings and sections section for how article is part of the document outline algorithm)

[08:27:00.0000] <ddfreyne>
I simply think the amount of new elements is too much

[08:28:00.0000] <ddfreyne>
I like <m> and <section>, but I don't think it's worth adding 10 more elements

[08:28:01.0000] <zcorpan_>
(2) i don't think it breaks anything (the content is still accessible as if the tags weren't there, no different from say <label>), it just isn't possible to style in some browsers

[08:29:00.0000] <ddfreyne>
